Luz Garcini, PhD, MPHLuz Garcini, PhD, MPH (She/Her/Ella) 1st (She/Her/Ella) 1st Clinical Health Psychologist/Epidemiologist/Researcher/Writer/Public Speaker/Advocate/Organizational and Community Consultant/Assistant ProfessorClinical Health Psychologist/Epidemiologist/Researcher/Writer/Public Speaker/Advocate/Organizational and Community Consultant/Assistant Professor
14h Edited 14h Edited
U.S. residents are more likely to die younger, and from avoidable causes, than residents of peer countries, according to a 2023 report from The Commonwealth Fund.

Researchers found the U.S. ranks last on four of five domains:
access to care (last)
administrative efficiency (last)
equity (last)
health care outcomes (last)
care process

In the face of growing health disparities and inequities, addressing non-medical drivers of health is critical.

#healthequity #healthcare #sdoh
Amelie RamirezAmelie Ramirez 2nd 2nd Professor at UT Health Science Center at SAProfessor at UT Health Science Center at SA
6d 6d
The health landscape is continually shifting with growing research on medical devices and non-medical factors.
Thus, comparing outcomes with peer countries is important to shed light on the best medical and NON-medical practices behind why some countries might be more successful than others.
Why are Other Nations Outperforming America on Health Outcomes? - Salud America
salud-america.org 5 min read
